<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 现有LLM智能体通常是单次问题求解器，无法从过去交互中学习。虽然从经验中提炼可复用技能是实现自我进化的自然途径，但高质量技能策展是关键瓶颈。现有方法依赖人工策展、启发式操作或短期训练，难以从间接延迟反馈中学习复杂的长期策展策略。

Method: SkillOS采用经验驱动的RL训练框架，包含冻结的智能体执行器（检索和应用技能）和可训练的技能策展器（更新外部SkillRepo）。设计复合奖励函数，并在基于技能相关任务依赖的分组任务流上训练，早期轨迹更新SkillRepo，后期相关任务评估更新效果。

Result: 在多轮智能体任务和单轮推理任务上，SkillOS在有效性和效率上均持续优于无记忆和强记忆基线方法，且学到的技能策展器可跨不同执行器骨干和任务领域泛化。分析表明策展器产生更精准的技能使用，SkillRepo中的技能随训练演化为结构更丰富的Markdown文件，编码更高级的元技能。

Conclusion: SkillOS通过强化学习有效解决了从延迟反馈中学习长期技能策展策略的挑战，为LLM智能体的自我进化提供了可行方案，且具有良好的泛化能力。

Abstract: LLM-based agents are increasingly deployed to handle streaming tasks, yet they often remain one-off problem solvers that fail to learn from past interactions. Reusable skills distilled from experience provide a natural substrate for self-evolution, where high-quality skill curation serves as the key bottleneck. Existing approaches either rely on manual skill curation, prescribe heuristic skill operations, or train for short-horizon skill operations. However, they still struggle to learn complex long-term curation policies from indirect and delayed feedback. To tackle this challenge, we propose SkillOS, an experience-driven RL training recipe for learning skill curation in self-evolving agents. SkillOS pairs a frozen agent executor that retrieves and applies skills with a trainable skill curator that updates an external SkillRepo from accumulated experience. To provide learning signals for curation, we design composite rewards and train on grouped task streams based on skill-relevant task dependencies, where earlier trajectories update the SkillRepo, and later related tasks evaluate these updates. Across multi-turn agentic tasks and single-turn reasoning tasks, SkillOS consistently outperforms memory-free and strong memory-based baselines in both effectiveness and efficiency, with the learned skill curator generalizing across different executor backbones and task domains. Further analyses show that the learned curator produces more targeted skill use, while the skills in SkillRepo evolve into more richly structured Markdown files that encode higher-level meta-skills over time.

</details>


### [421] [MASPO: Joint Prompt Optimization for LLM-based Multi-Agent Systems](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.06623)
*Zhexuan Wang,Xuebo Liu,Li Wang,Zifei Shan,Yutong Wang,Zhenxi Song,Min Zhang*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: MASPO是一个面向基于LLM的多智能体系统的自动化提示词优化框架，通过联合评估机制和数据驱动的进化波束搜索，迭代优化整个系统中所有智能体的提示词，实现局部目标与全局效果的对齐，在6个任务上平均提升2.9%准确率。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 在多智能体系统中，每个智能体的提示词质量至关重要，但联合优化多个交互智能体的提示词极具挑战性，因为局部智能体目标与整体系统目标之间存在不对齐问题。现有方法缺乏自动、迭代地优化全系统提示词的能力。

Method: MASPO包含两大核心创新：(1) 联合评估机制——不仅评估提示词的局部有效性，还评估其对后续智能体下游任务成功的贡献，弥合局部交互与全局效果之间的鸿沟；(2) 数据驱动的进化波束搜索——高效导航高维提示词空间，实现自动迭代优化。

Result: 在6个不同任务上的广泛实验表明，MASPO持续优于现有最优提示词优化方法，平均准确率提升2.9%。

Conclusion: MASPO有效解决了多智能体系统中提示词联合优化的难题，通过联合评估机制实现了局部目标与全局效果的对齐，为复杂协作任务中的自动提示词优化提供了新范式。

Abstract: Large language model (LLM)-based Multi-agent systems (MAS) have shown promise in tackling complex collaborative tasks, where agents are typically orchestrated via role-specific prompts. While the quality of these prompts is pivotal, jointly optimizing them across interacting agents remains a non-trivial challenge, primarily due to the misalignment between local agent objectives and holistic system goals. To address this, we introduce MASPO, a novel framework designed to automatically and iteratively refine prompts across the entire system. A core innovation of MASPO is its joint evaluation mechanism, which assesses prompts not merely by their local validity, but by their capacity to facilitate downstream success for successor agents. This effectively bridges the gap between local interactions and global outcomes without relying on ground-truth labels. Furthermore, MASPO employs a data-driven evolutionary beam search to efficiently navigate the high-dimensional prompt space. Extensive empirical evaluations across 6 diverse tasks demonstrate that MASPO consistently outperforms state-of-the-art prompt optimization methods, achieving an average accuracy improvement of 2.9. We release our code at https://github.com/wangzx1219/MASPO.

</details>


### [422] [Can RL Teach Long-Horizon Reasoning to LLMs? Expressiveness Is Key](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.06638)
*Tianle Wang,Zhaoyang Wang,Guangchen Lan,Xinpeng Wei,Sipeng Zhang,Guanwen Qiu,Abulhair Saparov*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: 本文提出ScaleLogic框架，通过控制推理深度和逻辑表达力两个维度，系统研究RL训练大模型推理的规模规律，发现训练计算量随推理深度呈幂律增长（T ∝ D^γ），且指数γ随逻辑表达力单调递增（1.04→2.60）。更具表达力的训练设置在下游数学和推理基准上带来更大性能提升（最高+10.66点）和更高效的计算迁移。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: RL已用于提升LLM推理能力，但缺乏可控、可扩展的环境来系统研究训练规模如何随任务难度变化，现有工作难以独立控制推理深度和逻辑表达力这两个难度维度。

Method: 提出ScaleLogic合成逻辑推理框架，可独立控制推理深度（证明规划的horizon）和逻辑表达力（从简单蕴含逻辑到一阶谓词逻辑）。在该框架下进行RL训练，拟合计算量与深度之间的幂律关系，并跨多种RL方法和课程学习策略验证。

Result: RL训练计算量T与推理深度D呈幂律关系（R²>0.99），指数γ从蕴含逻辑的1.04单调增长到一阶逻辑的2.60。更具表达力的训练设置在下游数学和推理任务上取得更大性能提升（最高+10.66点），且计算迁移效率更高。幂律关系在多种RL方法下成立，课程学习可显著提升扩展效率。

Conclusion: 模型训练的内容（逻辑表达力）与训练量同等重要，甚至更影响下游迁移效果；推理深度与计算量之间存在可预测的幂律关系，为LLM推理训练的规模扩展提供了理论指导。

Abstract: Reinforcement learning (RL) has been applied to improve large language model (LLM) reasoning, yet the systematic study of how training scales with task difficulty has been hampered by the lack of controlled, scalable environments. We introduce ScaleLogic, a synthetic logical reasoning framework that offers independent control over two axes of difficulty: the depth of the required proof planning (i.e., the horizon) and the expressiveness of the underlying logic. Our proposed framework supports a wide range of logics: from simple implication-only logic ("if-then") towards more expressive first-order reasoning with conjunction ("and"), disjunction ("or"), negation ("not"), and universal quantification ("for all"). Using this framework, we show that the RL training compute $T$ follows a power law with respect to reasoning depth $D$ ($T \propto D^γ$, $R^{2} > 0.99$), and that the scaling exponent $γ$ increases monotonically with logical expressiveness, from $1.04$ to $2.60$. On downstream mathematics and general reasoning benchmarks, more expressive training settings yield both larger performance gains (up to $+10.66$ points) and more compute-efficient transfer compared to less expressive settings, demonstrating that what a model is trained on, not just how much it is trained, shapes downstream transfer. We further show that the power-law relationship holds across multiple RL methods, and curriculum-based training substantially improves scaling efficiency.

</details>


### [423] [GlazyBench: A Benchmark for Ceramic Glaze Property Prediction and Image Generation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.06641)
*Ziyu Zhai,Siyou Li,Juexi Shao,Juntao Yu*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: 本文提出了GlazyBench，首个用于AI辅助陶瓷釉料设计的数据集，包含23,148个真实釉料配方，支持釉料表面属性预测和可视化生成两个任务，并建立了传统机器学习、大语言模型、深度生成模型及多模态模型的基准测试。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 陶瓷釉料开发依赖昂贵且耗时的试错过程，独立艺术家负担沉重；尽管多模态AI提供了现代解决方案，但该领域缺乏训练这些模型所需的大规模数据集。

Method: 构建了包含23,148个真实釉料配方的GlazyBench数据集；定义了两个核心任务（属性预测与可视化生成）；使用传统机器学习、大语言模型进行属性预测基准测试，使用深度生成模型和多模态大模型进行图像生成基准测试。

Result: 实验结果表明该方法具有前景但仍有挑战性，具体性能结果文中未详细展开。

Conclusion: GlazyBench开创了AI辅助材料设计的新研究方向，为系统评估提供了标准化基准。

Abstract: Developing ceramic glazes is a costly, time-consuming process of trial and error due to complex chemistry, placing a significant burden on independent artists. While recent advances in multimodal AI offer a modern solution, the field lacks the large-scale datasets required to train these models. We propose GlazyBench, the first dataset for AI-assisted glaze design. Comprising 23,148 real glaze formulations, GlazyBench supports two primary tasks: predicting post-firing surface properties, such as color and transparency, from raw materials, and generating accurate visual representations of the glaze based on these properties. We establish comprehensive baselines for property prediction using traditional machine learning and large language models, alongside image generation benchmarks using deep generative and large multimodal models. Our experiments demonstrate promising yet challenging results. GlazyBench pioneers a new research direction in AI-assisted material design, providing a standardized benchmark for systematic evaluation.

</details>


### [424] [AI Co-Mathematician: Accelerating Mathematicians with Agentic AI](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.06651)
*Daniel Zheng,Ingrid von Glehn,Yori Zwols,Iuliya Beloshapka,Lars Buesing,Daniel M. Roy,Martin Wattenberg,Bogdan Georgiev,Tatiana Schmidt,Andrew Cowie,Fernanda Viegas,Dimitri Kanevsky,Vineet Kahlon,Hartmut Maennel,Sophia Alj,George Holland,Alex Davies,Pushmeet Kohli*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: 提出AI合著数学家（AI co-mathematician）工作台，通过交互式AI代理为数学家提供开放式研究全流程支持，在FrontierMath Tier 4上取得48%的新最高分。


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: 现有AI数学系统多聚焦于单一任务（如定理证明或计算），缺乏对数学家实际工作中探索性、迭代性工作流的整体支持。需要一种能管理不确定性、细化用户意图、追踪失败假设并产出原生数学产物的交互式系统。

Method: 构建异步、有状态的工作台系统，集成AI代理以支持构思、文献搜索、计算探索、定理证明和理论构建五大模块；通过状态化管理用户意图和失败假设，模拟人类协作工作流。

Result: 辅助研究人员解决开放问题、发现新研究方向、挖掘被忽视的文献；在FrontierMath Tier 4基准上达到48%准确率，创下所有AI系统评估中的新纪录。

Conclusion: AI合著数学家展示了高交互范式在AI辅助数学发现中的有效性，为开放式数学研究提供了可落地的协作工具，并在硬性解题基准上达到业界领先水平。

Abstract: We introduce the AI co-mathematician, a workbench for mathematicians to interactively leverage AI agents to pursue open-ended research. The AI co-mathematician is optimized to provide holistic support for the exploratory and iterative reality of mathematical workflows, including ideation, literature search, computational exploration, theorem proving and theory building. By providing an asynchronous, stateful workspace that manages uncertainty, refines user intent, tracks failed hypotheses, and outputs native mathematical artifacts, the system mirrors human collaborative workflows. In early tests, the AI co-mathematician helped researchers solve open problems, identify new research directions, and uncover overlooked literature references. Besides demonstrating a highly interactive paradigm for AI-assisted mathematical discovery, the AI co-mathematician also achieves state of the art results on hard problem-solving benchmarks, including scoring 48% on FrontierMath Tier 4, a new high score among all AI systems evaluated.

</details>
